<a id="paper-2605.04812"></a>
### [Role of mass fluctuations in the diffusion of clusters of Brownian particles with activity](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04812v1)

**Authors:** Daniela Moretti, Pasquale Digregorio, Giuseppe Gonnella, Antonio Suma  
**Type:** both · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.04812v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **3/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.04812_figures/2605.04812_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 1: (a) Time evolution of a stationary cluster of N(t) particles, taken from an ABPs simulation with a total of 3025 particles (cluster mean size N0 = 2036 as black line) and (b) corresponding probability distribution P(N), see SM for simulation details. The yellow shaded region marks the range where N fluctuates within 10% of N0; within this region P(N) is approximately Gaussian (black line fit in (b)). (c) Snapshots at two consecutive close times (left to right) with particles lost from the left snapshots highlighted in red; top (bottom) row shows a mass-change event inside (outside) the yellow region of (a). (d) Cluster’s diffusion coefficient D versus mean cluster size N0 from ABP...</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.04812_figures/2605.04812_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 2: (a) Schematic of fragment attachment to the main cluster. The fragment (center-of-mass r∆N CM) and the main cluster (center-of-mass rN CM) are connected by the vector dcm = |dcm|ζ, where ζ is a random unit vector drawn from the surface of a d-dimensional sphere and |dcm| equals the sum of the two radii. Projections of the centers of mass along an arbitrary direction rCM,a are also shown. (b) Rescaled probability distributions P(N) from ABP simulations at different mean cluster sizes N0. The solid line is the standard normal distribution N(0, 1). (c) Variance σ2 N versus mean cluster size N0, extracted from the distributions in (b). The solid line is a power-law fit pN β 0 with β =...</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2605.04812_figures/2605.04812_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 3: Diffusion coefficient D versus mean cluster size N0, as given by Eq. (18), using Da = 8.33, d = 2 (same value as ABPs simulations, see SM). (a) Fixed Dg = 1.4 (from fitted ABPs simulation values); and different values of δ. (b) Fixed δ = 0.63 and different values of Dg.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper provides a theoretical explanation for the anomalous diffusion of active particle clusters by accounting for the stochastic fluctuations in cluster mass due to particle attachment and detachment. It demonstrates that these mass fluctuations create a new diffusion contribution that dominates at large cluster sizes, leading to the observed non-standard scaling.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Explaining the origin of anomalous diffusion in the center-of-mass of clusters of Active Brownian Particles (ABPs), specifically why the diffusion coefficient scales as D ~ N^(-1/2) instead of the conventional N^(-1).

**Main result.** The authors derive a theoretical framework showing that the diffusion coefficient is the sum of a conventional term and a fluctuation-driven term arising from mass exchange, predicting an anomalous scaling exponent alpha = 0.63 +/- 0.06 that matches simulations.

**Method.** The study combines an analytical derivation using coupled stochastic Langevin equations with large-scale numerical simulations of Active Brownian Particles.

**Model / system.** The system consists of clusters of Active Brownian Particles (ABPs) undergoing Motility-induced Phase Separation (MIPS), modeled using Active Ornstein-Uhlenbeck Particles (AOUPs) to account for mass exchange (attachment/detachment) with the surrounding phase.

**Key observables.** Center-of-mass diffusion coefficient (D), Mean-Square Displacement (MSD), cluster mass evolution N(t), and scaling exponents (alpha, beta, kappa, delta).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Mean cluster size (N0), mass fluctuation variance scaling (beta), mass fluctuation persistence time (kappa), and spatial dimension (d).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The mass evolution N(t) follows a Gaussian process; clusters are assumed to be roughly spherical; mass fluctuations are small relative to the total mass (|delta N| < N).

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows cluster dynamics and mass exchange snapshots; Figure 2 illustrates the schematic of fragment attachment/detachment and fits for the diffusion exponents; Figure 3 shows the diffusion coefficient scaling with cluster size in 2D.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of anomalous diffusion, presents a theoretical framework based on coupled stochastic equations for COM and mass, validates the model against ABP simulations, and discusses the scaling regimes and dimensionality effects.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Motivated by the anomalous diffusion observed in clusters of active Brownian particles (ABPs), where the center-of-mass diffusion coefficient scales as $D\sim N^{-1/2}$ with respect to the number $N$ of particles in the cluster, we derive a minimal theoretical framework starting from the single-particle Langevin equations. The model consists of two coupled stochastic equations: one for the cluster center-of-mass trajectory and one for the mass evolution $N(t)$, explicitly accounting for stochastic displacements induced by particle attachment and detachment. We specialize and validate the framework against ABP simulations of isolated clusters in stationary conditions, where $N(t)$ follows a Gaussian process with mean $N_0$, variance $\propto N_0^β$, and persistence time $\propto N_0^κ$. Analytical solution of the coupled equations yields the long-time diffusion coefficient as the sum of two contributions: a conventional term $\propto N_0^{-1}$) due to thermal noise plus summation of active forces, and a fluctuation-driven term $\propto N_0^{-δ}$ with $δ=2-2/d-β+κ$, where $d$ is the spatial dimension. We demonstrate that anomalous scaling emerges whenever the second term becomes dominant. The model predicts $D\sim N^{-α}$ with $α=0.63\pm0.06$, in good quantitative agreement with large-scale ABP simulations.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.04538"></a>
### [Second quantization of anyons and spin-anyon duality](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04538v1)

**Authors:** Priyanshi Bhasin, Diptiman Sen, Tanmoy Das  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** strongly correlated electrons · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.04538v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `analog quantum simulation` **3/5** · `exotic spin models in light-matter` **3/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.04538_figures/2605.04538_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 1. Schematic of an anyon chain with PBC. The PBC is imposed by a phase (M −1)θ which can be either inserted in the Hamiltonian or many-body state. Here we can impose the phase either at a given site (left panel), or distribute it equally on each bond as (M−1)θ/L (right panel). The advantage of the second approach, as done here, is that it makes the total momentum a good quantum number.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.04538_figures/2605.04538_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 2. Persistent current and energy gap as a func- tion of filling fraction (ν), hopping amplitude (t), and onsite interaction strength (U). Left panel: (a) En- ergy gap between the first excited state and the ground state ∆E = E1 −E0 is plotted as a heatmap as a function of ν and t/U. The fixed parameters are ∆1 = 1, ∆2 = 4, and the system size is L = 17. White regions denote the sup- pression or closing of the energy gap. The dark blue column at ν = 1 denotes a very large gap ∆E ∼O(U). (b) The corresponding ground-state persistent current ⟨J⟩0 is shown at the same parameter values. Red and blue regions indicate positive and negative currents, respectively, while the white region denotes...</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2605.04538_figures/2605.04538_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 3. Energy gap and persistent current. (a) Energy gap ∆(upper panel), and (b) the ground state current ⟨J⟩0 (lower panel), plotted as a function of anyon number density ν , at fixed t = 0.4, ∆1 = 1, and ∆2 = 4 (i.e., U = 2 &gt; 0). Dots represent computed data and the lines are guides to the eyes. The vertical dashed line marks half-filling (M = L). The sign reversals in ⟨J⟩0 are associate with minima in ∆E.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2605.04538_figures/2605.04538_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 2 consolidates these level inversions in the M versus t parameter space. We notice that despite the βn = βN−n symmetry, the symmetry across half-filling is not always present in the phase diagram. This is due to the ∆2 ̸= ∆1 parameter value, which imbalances the energy cost for double versus single anyon occupancies. Interestingly, all discontinuous jumps in the current are diagnosed with a level inversion, rather than any non- analyticity in the ground state. There are multiple level crossings along the ν, while the level crossings along the t axis for fixed ν is limited to a narrow window near ν ∼1/4 and ∼3/4 regions.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2605.04538_figures/2605.04538_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 5. Two point correlation functions. We show the imaginary parts of the equal time correlation functions: (a) Gij corresponds to ‘Green’s’ function G0i for anyons, and (b) χ+− ij gives transverse spin correlation function. We set i = 0 and plot as a function of j →j. We show results for two representative values of t across critical hopping tc = 0.4, ν ∼0.6, ∆1 = 1, and ∆2 = 4. For t &lt; tc, all curves corresponding to t ∈[0.36, 0.39] overlap exactly. Similarly, the curves corresponding to t ≥tc for t ∈[0.40, 0.43] are also exactly overlapping. Both correlation functions exhibit spatial modulation, with a sudden change in amplitude and wavevector at tc.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper presents a new second-quantized algebraic framework for 1D Abelian anyons that correctly accounts for both finite on-site occupancy and non-local exchange phases. It demonstrates an exact duality between pi/3 anyons and spin-1 operators, allowing anyonic models to be mapped to spin-1 XY-like models. This provides a new method for realizing anyonic statistics in physical systems like spin chains.

**Why it may be interesting.** The establishment of a duality between anyonic statistics and spin-1 operators offers a concrete theoretical pathway to engineer anyonic physics using well-understood spin-1 lattice models and synthetic gauge fields.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Developing a consistent second-quantized formulation for Abelian anyons that simultaneously enforces local exclusion rules (finite on-site occupancy) and non-local exchange/braiding phases.

**Main result.** The authors establish a new algebraic framework for 1D anyons and an exact Jordan-Wigner duality between pi/3 anyons and spin-1 operators, providing a route to realize anyons via spin Hamiltonians.

**Method.** The study uses deformed commutation relations, a modified Jordan-Wigner transformation, and Exact Diagonalization (ED) via the QuSpin package to analyze the resulting spin-1 models.

**Model / system.** A 1D lattice of Abelian anyons with statistical phase theta = pi/N, featuring a tight-binding Hamiltonian with density-dependent phases and an on-site Hubbard-like interaction.

**Key observables.** Ground-state energy, total momentum, persistent current, energy gap, ground-state fidelity, and two-point correlation functions.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Statistical angle theta, anyon density (filling fraction) nu, hopping amplitude t, Hubbard interaction U, and site occupancy limit N-1.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The algebraic construction and many-body states are restricted to 1D chains; the study focuses on Abelian anyons.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows a schematic of anyon chains with periodic boundary conditions; Figure 6 and 7 illustrate anyon exchange processes and phase accumulation; Figure 8 plots the energy gap and persistent current as functions of anyon density for even and odd system sizes.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces a new algebraic framework for anyon second quantization, establishes a spin-anyon duality for the pi/3 case, performs numerical analysis of the resulting models using ED, and provides consistency checks via various exchange processes.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Anyons exhibit a non-trivial interplay between local exclusion rules and non-local braiding and exchange phases, making a consistent commutation algebra and second-quantized formulation challenging. We develop an algebraic framework for Abelian anyons in one dimension with statistical phase $θ$ = $π$/N that enforces a finite on-site occupancy of N-1 anyons with the exchange phase $θ$ between different sites. Moreover, we introduce an exact Jordan-Wigner duality between $π$/3 anyons and spin-1 operators, allowing us to map a tight-binding anyon model to an XY-like spin-1 model. The model exhibits anyon-density-dependent flux, incompressible or gapless regions, and critical points with level crossings that appear as discontinuities in ground-state currents, momenta, fidelities, and correlation functions. Our second-quantization formalism establishes a novel spin anyon duality, offering a conceptually new route to realize anyons from spin Hamiltonians and to engineer corresponding device architectures.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.05171"></a>
### [Plasma effects on lifetimes and screening of Rydberg excitons](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.05171v1)

**Authors:** AbdAlGhaffar Amer, V. Walther, Francis Robicheaux  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.05171v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **3/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.05171_figures/2605.05171_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>

The simulations are performed for increasing number of plasma charges N. Also shown is the same ratio for the Debye model. Increasing the number of plasma charges increases the range over which the results are in agreement with the Debye model. The used parameters are ρ = 0.5 × 1017 m−3 and Γ = 0.1.</sub>

</details>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper explores how a background plasma influences the stability and screening of Rydberg excitons in Cu2O. It demonstrates that because excitons move faster than the plasma can respond, standard Debye screening models fail to accurately describe the system. The findings provide a potential explanation for observed deviations in exciton lifetime scaling at high quantum numbers.

**Why it may be interesting.** It addresses the breakdown of the adiabatic (Debye) approximation in systems where internal particle dynamics are faster than the environment's response, which is highly relevant to open quantum systems and many-body dynamics.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how a neutral electron-hole plasma affects the lifetimes and screening of Rydberg excitons in cuprous oxide (Cu2O), specifically testing the validity of the Debye screening model.

**Main result.** The study finds that plasma-induced scattering causes exciton lifetimes to scale with density, temperature, and principal quantum number, and that Debye screening overestimates the screening of the exciton's internal field due to high orbital frequencies.

**Method.** The authors use a combination of a classical orbit model and a semiclassical approach using the Truncated Wigner Approximation (TWA) to evolve the exciton state.

**Model / system.** A neutral electron-hole plasma interacting with Rydberg excitons in cuprous oxide (Cu2O), where excitons are modeled as classical Keplerian orbits or quantum harmonic oscillators.

**Key observables.** Exciton lifetime (tau), Debye screening length, electric field ratio (simulated vs. unscreened), and plasma-induced scattering rates.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Principal quantum number (n), plasma density (rho), temperature (T), and the adiabaticity ratio (omega_Ryd/omega_p).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The plasma is treated as a weakly correlated classical system (Gamma <= 0.2), and quantum correlations between electrons and holes are neglected.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 validates the plasma model via Debye screening; Figure 2 shows exciton lifetime scaling with density; Figure 6 shows normalized lifetime vs. frequency ratio; Figure 8 presents a rho-T phase diagram of exciton observability and screening limits.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by validating the plasma simulation against known Debye screening, moves to modeling exciton dynamics via classical and semiclassical methods, analyzes lifetime scaling and spectral loss mechanisms, and concludes with an analysis of screening efficiency and a phase diagram of exciton stability.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We simulate the effects of a neutral electron--hole plasma on Rydberg excitons in cuprous oxide (Cu$_2$O), focusing on the validity of Debye screening and the role of plasma-induced thermalization. Unlike atomic Rydberg states, excitons in Cu$_2$O consist of quasiparticles with comparable effective masses whose orbital frequencies can exceed the plasma frequency, invalidating the assumption of a stationary screened charge. Using two complementary approaches, a classical orbit model and a harmonic-oscillator representation evolved via the truncated Wigner approximation, we study exciton lifetimes and interaction screening under realistic plasma conditions. We find numerically that plasma-induced scattering induces finite exciton lifetimes with specific scaling relations with plasma density, principal quantum number $n$ and temperature, possibly providing an explanation for experimentally observed deviations from the $n^3$ scaling at high principal quantum numbers. By explicitly computing time-averaged electric fields, we show that Debye screening overestimates the screening of the exciton's internal field, especially for high angular momentum states. Furthermore, we demonstrate that exciton-exciton interactions are not Debye screened at separations comparable to the Debye length for Rydberg excitons that are well resolvable in absorption measurements.

</details>

<sub>FIG. 6: Illustration of (a): Eq. (32) and (b): Eq. (36) for the group G15,2. In both cases, the cosets generated by Ci aNGN (Figure (a)) and Ci aNGa (Figure (b)) are depicted using the same color. For example, in Figure (a), the action of all Ci+ja aN ; ∀j = [0, N −1], on GN, for odd or even values of i yields either the black or the white regions. **Summary.** This paper demonstrates that the mathematical structure of Shor's algorithm can be mapped onto the physical symmetries of molecules and periodic lattices. By showing that prime factors are encoded in the Fourier modes of these systems, it suggests that engineered matter could potentially be used to solve hard mathematical problems.

**Why it may be interesting.** It proposes a novel bridge between abstract quantum algorithms and tangible physical symmetries in matter, suggesting that synthetic molecular or lattice engineering could serve as a platform for physicalized quantum computation.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating whether the group-theoretic structure of Shor's algorithm and the Hidden Subgroup Problem (HSP) can be physically realized using the symmetries of molecular and condensed-phase systems.

**Main result.** The authors establish a formal mathematical mapping between the modular arithmetic used in Shor's algorithm and the periodic symmetries found in molecular orbitals and Bloch wavefunctions, suggesting that physical systems could potentially encode prime-factor information.

**Method.** The study uses group theory, specifically representation theory, the Chinese Remainder Theorem, and projection operators, to relate cyclic group rotations to symmetry-adapted linear combinations (SALCs) and Bloch's theorem.

**Model / system.** The models include molecular systems (e.g., hexahydroxybenzene, polyenes), condensed-phase assemblies (periodic lattices, quantum corrals), and optical beams with specific angular momenta, all modeled via rotation groups and periodic potentials.

**Key observables.** The Fourier structure of molecular orbitals, Bloch phases, and the period 'r' of the modular exponentiation function.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The integer N to be factored, its prime factors b_i, and the subdivision factor 'a' used to define the extended group G_{N,a}.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The experimental realization of these engineered systems remains an open question; the model assumes electrons in polyene systems exist in a periodic 1D potential extending to the required residues.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate quantum circuit templates, the step-by-step correspondence between Shor's algorithm and physical symmetries, visual representations of group rotations and molecular structures (like hexahydroxybenzene), and the division of groups into cosets.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by defining modular arithmetic as a rotation group, develops the representation theory for these groups, formulates the HSP, and then establishes the structural correspondence to molecular orbitals and Bloch wavefunctions.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We describe a group theoretic analysis of Shor's algorithm and other related hidden subgroup problems in mathematics and relate these to symmetries of molecular and condensed phase assemblies. By recasting Shor's algorithm through the lens of group theory, we expose the possibility that physical systems such as molecular orbitals, condensed phase assemblies and optical beams may be designed such that these contain information pertaining to the solution to hard mathematical problems such as prime-factoring. We discuss real molecular systems, whose orbitals are constructed from symmetry-adapted linear combinations of atomic orbitals, and show that these contain information pertaining to the prime-factors of corresponding integers. Due to the broad significance of prime-factoring towards a variety of encryption problems in cyber-security, we believe this novel and fundamental approach may have broad impact.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.05158"></a>
### [The Saturable Electronic Reluctance Switch: Switchable low-power and low-noise generation of magnetic fields using permanent magnets](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.05158v1)

**Authors:** P. D. Taylor-Burdett, C. A. Burhan, S. Mason, F. R. Lebrun-Gallagher, S. Weidt, W. K. Hensinger  
**Type:** both · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.05158v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `QC/QI experiment` **3/5** · `spintronics-quantum-optics interface` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<sub>Fig. 1 Cross-section of a Saturable Electronic Reluctance Switch magnetic circuit, illustrating the operating principle in the low-field “OFF” (top) and high-field “ON” (bottom) states. Switching is actioned by driving two shunt cores into full saturation using anti-parallel solenoids. In the OFF- state, flux from a permanent magnet is directed through shunts with high magnetic permeability. When a driving current around the shunts is switched on, the shunts lose their permeability and the flux is instead directed towards an air-gap output region. By magnetising the shunts along a single axis, full saturation is achieved, ensuring perme- ability remains constant in the ON-state. The...</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.05158_figures/2605.05158_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 2 a) Schematic of a simple Saturable Electronic Reluctance Switch (SERS) device. The device contains a primary soft ferromagnetic core of cross-sectional area Ap that provides two paths, P1 and P2, for the magnetic flux, Φm, of a permanent magnet of length ℓm and area Am. P1 contains two high-permeability shunts, S1 and S2, of area As and length ℓs. Each shunt is tightly wound with an N-turn solenoid carrying current a ηnI, where ηn = (−1)n. P2 contains and air- gap of length ℓg and area Ag, where the experiment requiring a switchable field is located. b) An idealised magnetic circuit model of the device, excluding primary core reluctance.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

Switching is observed by the step-like transition from a linear ramp in the air-gap field to a nearly-constant field value as the applied current is increased. For an ideal SERS circuit, the initial linear ramp in air-gap field is given by κoff = µ0N/ℓg, as highlighted with a dashed line. The same two parameters are calculated for a non-linear...</sub>

Magnetic polarity is indicated by colour (blue/red). a) Ring core arrangement (RCA) structure, with prototype parameters of s = 0.2 mm, w = 0.5 mm, H = 5.5 mm and W = 8 mm. b) FEM simulated magnetic field magnitude in all three planes for the RCA core after magnetisation with cylindrical permanent magnets of remanent flux density Br =1 T, length ℓm =3 mm and radius rm =1 mm. c) Linear core arrangement (LCA) structure, with prototype parameters of s1 = 0.15 mm, s2 = 0.2 mm, w1 = 0.5 mm, w2 = 1 mm, D = 1 mm, H = 5.5 mm and W = 17.5 mm. <sub>Fig. 5 a) Schematic of a SERS-driven fringe field quadrupole core prototype for creating switchable ultra- low noise magnetic field gradients in the gate zone of a a trapped-ion quantum information processor. Here, the device is illustrated positioned underneath a gate zone region of surface trap, creating a field-gradient along the axial z-axis with quantisation direction along the x-axis. b) FEM simulation results of the magnetic field gradient mag- nitude produced at an ion height of 500 µm above the core surface as a function of driving current (orange). **Summary.** The paper introduces the Saturable Electronic Reluctance Switch (SERS), a device that uses non-linear ferromagnets to switch magnetic fields with extremely low noise and power consumption. By saturating a shunt path, the device can turn magnetic fields on and off while remaining insensitive to current fluctuations. This technology offers a scalable solution for generating stable magnetic field gradients in trapped-ion quantum computers.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for AMO physicists working on trapped-ion QCCD architectures, as it provides a way to implement high-gradient, low-noise magnetic control without the heating and noise penalties of traditional electromagnets.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The difficulty of generating magnetic fields that are simultaneously ultra-stable (low noise) and switchable (on/off) for applications like trapped-ion quantum computing.

**Main result.** The development of a Saturable Electronic Reluctance Switch (SERS) that reduces magnetic field noise from current fluctuations by up to five orders of magnitude and reduces power dissipation by an order of magnitude compared to conventional wires.

**Method.** The study uses analytical magnetic circuit modeling (reluctance-based) and 3D non-linear Finite Element Method (FEM) simulations via COMSOL Multiphysics to evaluate different material alloys and geometries.

**Model / system.** A hybrid magnetic circuit (SERS) consisting of a primary ferromagnetic core, a source magnet, and a shunt section with anti-parallel solenoids designed to switch flux between a shunt path and an air-gap.

**Key observables.** Current sensitivity (kappa), switching ratio (alpha), magnetic field gradient (partial B/partial z), and power dissipation (Joule losses).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Saturation threshold current (Isat), permeability (mu), saturation flux density (Bsat), and the switching ratio (alpha).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The primary core is assumed to have negligible reluctance; leakage flux is represented by a lumped parallel reluctance; and copper resistivity is assumed constant at 300 K.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows a cross-section of the SERS illustrating the OFF state; subsequent figures illustrate the SERS-driven quadrupole prototype and its integration with ion trap architectures.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the stability-switchability trade-off, describes the SERS physical mechanism and design conditions, presents numerical simulations of different materials and geometries, and concludes with a practical application for trapped-ion quantum computing.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Across many areas of science, there is a need to generate magnetic fields that are both ultra-stable and switchable on and off. While permanent and superconducting magnets offer exceptionally low-noise fields, they are not readily switchable. Conversely, electromagnets are switchable but are susceptible to current noise. We present a hybrid technique to switch the field of any arbitrary magnet through use of a non-linear ferromagnetic circuit, named the Saturable Electronic Reluctance Switch (SERS). The circuit achieves bi-stable switching of the field by applying a current above a given threshold, akin to a transistor for magnetic fields. Crucially, the applied current has minimal influence on the magnetic field output and demagnetisation of the magnet is avoided, drastically reducing power dissipation. SERS is also robust to fabrication errors, suppressing noise in the control current by several orders of magnitude in a non-ideal device. To illustrate its application, a SERS-driven device is proposed for generating ultra-stable magnetic field gradients in a scalable trapped-ion quantum computer. We find this device offers an order of magnitude reduction in power dissipation compared to state-of-the-art current carrying wires, while reducing magnetic field noise originating from current fluctuations by up to five orders of magnitude.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.04931"></a>
### [Quantum Realizability of Probabilistic Theories Stable under Teleportation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04931v1)

**Authors:** Miguel A. A. Lisboa  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.04931v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **1/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.04931_figures/2605.04931_page3.jpg" width="500"><br>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2605.04931_figures/2605.04931_page6.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 6</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper resolves the question of which teleportation-stable General Probabilistic Theories are compatible with standard quantum mechanics. By using group representation theory, the author proves that only two out of seven previously identified families are quantum-realizable. The study provides explicit constructions for these two families using Bell-basis measurements and POVMs.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides fundamental constraints on the types of probabilistic theories that can exist as quantum-mechanical systems, which is relevant for understanding the boundaries of quantum information protocols like teleportation.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper aims to determine which of the seven families of General Probabilistic Theories (GPTs) that are stable under teleportation and entanglement swapping can be physically realized within the framework of standard quantum mechanics.

**Main result.** The author proves that exactly two of the seven families are quantum-realizable (specifically χ^{K4}_{1234} and χ^{D4}_{125}), while the remaining five families admit no quantum realization.

**Method.** The study employs elementary representation theory, character tables of finite groups (K4, Z4, and D4), and the analysis of projective representations via the Schur cover (D8) to check for compatibility with unitary representations.

**Model / system.** The mathematical framework involves General Probabilistic Theories (GPTs) and their operator spaces, specifically analyzing the action of correction groups (K4, Z4, D4) on the algebra of operators in finite-dimensional Hilbert spaces.

**Key observables.** CHSH value, conjugation character (χ_conj), and the multiplicity of irreducible representations.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Dimensions of the Hilbert space and the character components of the group representations.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes finite-dimensional Hilbert spaces and focuses on the effective GPT classification provided by previous work.

**Figures summary.** Table I details the conjugacy classes of the dihedral group D4, and Table II summarizes the dimensions and character compositions of the seven GPT families.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by defining the problem of quantum realizability, uses representation theory to establish constraints on the multiplicity of characters, proves the impossibility of five families through dimension and multiplicity obstructions, and concludes by providing explicit quantum constructions for the two realizable families.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

The classification of general probabilistic theories (GPTs) whose CHSH value is stable under arbitrary rounds of teleportation and entanglement swapping was recently obtained in Dmello and Gross work and consists of seven families, indexed by characters of the Klein four-group $K_4$, the cyclic group $\mathbb{Z}_4$, and the dihedral group $D_4$. The question of which of these families admits a realization within standard quantum mechanics was left open. In this work we resolve this question completely. Using elementary representation theory, we prove that exactly two families are quantum-realizable, namely $χ^{K_4}_{1234}$ and $χ^{D_4}_{125}$, while the remaining five admit no quantum realization.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.04879"></a>
### [Catalytic advantage in asymptotic entanglement manipulation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04879v1)

**Authors:** Ray Ganardi  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.04879v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.04879_figures/2605.04879_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 1. An illustration of the catalytic protocol in Proposi- tion 1.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates that using a catalyst can significantly reduce the amount of entanglement needed to prepare many copies of a mixed state exactly. It establishes that this catalytic advantage in the asymptotic regime is fundamentally linked to the non-convexity of the exact entanglement cost. The findings are shown to be generalizable to other resource theories, such as the thermodynamic cost of work.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides fundamental insights into the irreversibility and resource manipulation limits in quantum information, specifically showing how auxiliary systems can fundamentally change the scaling of resource costs in the many-copy limit.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates whether catalysis (using an auxiliary state that is returned unchanged) can provide a significant advantage in reducing the exact entanglement cost in the asymptotic (many-copy) regime.

**Main result.** The author proves that catalysis can strictly lower the exact entanglement cost for mixed states in both PPT and LOCC frameworks, establishing that this advantage is a direct consequence of the non-convexity of the exact cost.

**Method.** The study uses the PPT entanglement theory as a proxy for LOCC, develops an explicit catalytic protocol using a SWAP operation, and employs mathematical tools like Jensen's Theorem and the properties of max-relative entropy.

**Model / system.** The work focuses on entanglement manipulation of mixed states, specifically Werner states and states with positive binegativity, using Bell pairs as the standard resource unit.

**Key observables.** Exact entanglement cost (E0c), catalytic exact entanglement cost (E0c,c), logarithmic negativity (LN), and exact work cost (W0c).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Asymptotic (many-copy) regime, single-copy regime, strict vs. correlated catalysis, and the distinction between exact and approximate cost regimes.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The advantage is analyzed in the 'exact' regime; the paper notes that the advantage may disappear in the 'approximate' regime where the cost function becomes convex.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates a catalytic protocol involving a sequence where a system state is transformed via a map followed by a SWAP operation with a catalyst.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of asymptotic catalysis, develops a mathematical framework using PPT and LOCC, provides an explicit protocol construction, proves the link between non-convexity and catalytic advantage, and generalizes the findings to other resource theories like thermodynamics.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Entanglement is a key quantum resource in various quantum protocols, with a rich set of laws governing its manipulation. In this context, catalysis refers to the possibility of an auxiliary state that enables a previously forbidden manipulation, while being completely returned at the end. While the catalytic setting has been thoroughly examined in the single-copy regime, much less is known in the asymptotically many copy regime. In this work, we focus on the entanglement cost of preparing asymptotically many copies of a given state exactly. We show that catalysis can significantly lower the exact entanglement cost by constructing an explicit catalytic protocol. Additionally, these findings generalize readily to other resource theories, showing a general catalytic advantage in the resource dilution task.

</details>

### [Search for magnetoacoustic quantum oscillations in the insulating phase of YbB$_{12}$](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04350v1)

**Summary.** This study uses ultrasonic measurements to search for magnetoacoustic quantum oscillations in the Kondo insulator YbB12. While oscillations were clearly seen in the field-induced metallic state, they were absent in the insulating state, providing critical constraints on the nature of potential neutral quasiparticles in this system.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating the origin of magnetic quantum oscillations in the insulating phase of the Kondo insulator YbB12 and determining if they arise from neutral quasiparticles or other exotic mechanisms.

**Main result.** Magnetoacoustic quantum oscillations were not observed in the insulating state, appearing only in the field-induced metallic phase, though some unexplained anomalies in elastic constants were detected in the insulating phase.

**Method.** Bulk-sensitive ultrasonic pulse-echo measurements in high magnetic fields (up to 65 T) and low temperatures (down to 485 mK), complemented by magnetoresistance and magnetocaloric effect measurements.

**Model / system.** The physical system is the Kondo insulator YbB12, characterized by a hybridization between 5d and 4f electrons, featuring an insulating phase at low fields and a field-induced metallic phase above approximately 45 T.

**Key observables.** Elastic constants (C11 and C44), ultrasonic velocities (v11 and v44), magnetoresistance (MR), and magnetocaloric effect (MCE).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Magnetic fields up to 65 T, temperatures down to 485 mK, cyclotron mass m* approx 15me, and oscillation frequency approx 700 T.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes the applicability of the Lifshitz-Kosevich formula to describe oscillatory contributions to the elastic constant.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the crystal structure and a phase diagram; Figure 4 illustrates the estimated upper bounds of the deformation potential and interaction strength.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of oscillations in insulators, describes the experimental setup and YbB12 sample, presents results for MR, MCE, and ultrasonic velocities, discusses the absence of oscillations in the insulating phase versus the metallic phase, and concludes with an analysis of the observed elastic anomalies.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

A highly exotic phenomenon in solid-state physics is the observation of magnetic quantum oscillations in insulators. For instance, in the Kondo insulator YbB$_{12}$ various groups reported the observation of such oscillations seemingly originating from Fermi surfaces, though this contradicts the concept of an insulator having no charged quasiparticles. In this study, we searched for quantum oscillations in YbB$_{12}$ by using bulk-sensitive ultrasonic experiments in high magnetic fields up to 65 T and down to 485 mK. For that, we utilized an YbB$_{12}$ single crystal that, in previous experiments, revealed oscillations in the magnetoresistance in the insulating state. We confirmed oscillation-like behavior of the magnetoresistance as well as field-dependent oscillations in the magnetocaloric effect. However, we could not observe magnetoacoustic quantum oscillations in the insulating state, only in the field-induced metallic state. In the insulating state, we found some anomalies in our ultrasound data, the origin of which remains elusive. Our findings provide further information on the puzzling behavior of the insulating state of YbB$_{12}$.

</details>

### [Stability and dynamics of dark-bright solitons in spin-orbit- and Rabi-coupled binary Bose-Einstein condensates](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04441v1)

**Summary.** This paper explores how spin-orbit and Rabi couplings modify the stability and dynamics of dark-bright solitons in two-component Bose-Einstein condensates. It reveals that while these couplings break the integrability of the system, they also enable the creation of complex nonlinear phenomena like breathing stripes and soliton fragmentation. The findings highlight the potential for using synthetic gauge fields to precisely control nonlinear structures in ultracold atoms.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides deep insights into how synthetic gauge fields and coherent coupling can be used to engineer and control nonlinear excitations and complex pattern formation in multicomponent quantum gases.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating the stability and nonlinear dynamics of dark-bright solitons in a binary Bose-Einstein condensate subjected to synthetic spin-orbit and Rabi couplings.

**Main result.** The study demonstrates that spin-orbit coupling breaks integrability and induces spatial separation and density oscillations, while Rabi coupling promotes phase locking and breather-like excitations; interaction quenches further drive the system into complex regimes like multi-soliton fragmentation and stripe patterns.

**Method.** Numerical simulations using imaginary-time propagation for ground states, real-time evolution via Split-Step Crank-Nicolson, and Bogoliubov-de Gennes analysis for stability and excitation spectra.

**Model / system.** A one-dimensional, pseudo-spin-1/2 binary Bose-Einstein condensate described by coupled Gross-Pitaevskii equations featuring spin-orbit coupling (kL), Rabi coupling (Omega), and inter/intraspecies interactions.

**Key observables.** Component densities, chemical potentials, energy functionals, population imbalance, and Bogoliubov-de Gennes excitation spectra (eigenfrequencies).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Spin-orbit coupling strength (kL), Rabi coupling strength (Omega), interaction strengths (g_ij), and external harmonic confinement vs. homogeneous (trapless) regimes.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is treated in a quasi-one-dimensional regime with strong transverse confinement; the study focuses on the nonlinear dynamics of the Gross-Pitaevskii framework.

**Figures summary.** Figures show ground-state density transitions (miscible to immiscible), soliton profiles in harmonic traps, spatiotemporal evolution of densities under increasing coupling strengths, and complex patterns (fragmentation, stripes) following interaction quenches in both trapped and free space.

**Paper structure.** The paper establishes a theoretical benchmark using the integrable Manakov model, analyzes the impact of spin-orbit and Rabi couplings on soliton stability via BdG analysis, and explores non-equilibrium dynamics through real-time simulations of interaction and coupling quenches.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We investigate the stability and nonlinear dynamics of dark-bright solitons in a one-dimensional binary Bose-Einstein condensate subjected to synthetic spin-orbit and Rabi couplings. In the absence of spin-orbit coupling, we map the coupled Gross-Pitaevskii equations onto the integrable Manakov model and obtain exact dark-bright soliton solutions, providing a rigorous theoretical benchmark. We demonstrate that finite spin-orbit coupling breaks integrability by inducing spin-dependent phase gradients, which result in spatial separation of the spin components and the emergence of intrinsic density oscillations. By contrast, Rabi coupling enforces phase locking between components and supports robust breather-like excitations. Using imaginary-time propagation together with Bogoliubov-de Gennes analysis, we systematically characterise ground-state phases and excitation spectra for both symmetric and asymmetric interaction regimes in homogeneous and harmonically trapped systems. Real-time simulations further demonstrate that finite gauge fields and interaction quenches drive the system far from equilibrium, giving rise to diverse nonlinear phenomena, including multi-soliton fragmentation, breathing stripe patterns, and soliton dynamics. Our results highlight the interplay of synthetic gauge fields, external confinement, and interaction engineering as powerful tools for controlling the stability and dynamical behaviour of nonlinear excitations in multicomponent quantum gases.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.05194"></a>
### [Singular Behavior of Observables at Hopf Bifurcations](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.05194v1)

**Authors:** Benedikt Remlein, Massimiliano Esposito  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.05194v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.05194_figures/2605.05194_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 1. Observable singularities at bifurcations. (a) Stationary bi- furcations transmit nonanalytic behavior through the critical sta- tionary branch 𝑥∗(𝜇). Smooth observables inherit the same lead- ing singularity under composition, e.g., 𝐴(𝑥∗(𝜇)) −𝐴(𝑥𝑐) ∼𝜇𝛽for 𝑥∗(𝜇) −𝑥𝑐∼𝜇𝛽, or inherit jumps under discontinuous branch selec- tion. (b) Supercritical Hopf bifurcation. The stationary branch re- mains smooth, while a stable limit cycle emerges for 𝜇&gt; 0 with am- plitude 𝑟∗∼𝜇1/2. The phase portraits illustrate the transition from a stable fixed point (𝜇&lt; 0) to periodic motion (𝜇&gt; 0), corresponding to spontaneous breaking of continuous time-translation symmetry. (c) Generic Hopf case for the...</sub>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.05194_figures/2605.05194_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 2. Numerical realizations of universal observable singularities in the vicinity of a Hopf bifurcation. Main panels show excess ob- servables, while insets display the lowest derivative that becomes discontinuous at the bifurcation. (a) Reversible Brusselator: the excess semi-grand Gibbs free energy belongs to the generic kink class. (b) CMOS ring oscillator (𝑁= 3): cancellation of the linear term...</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates that supercritical Hopf bifurcations act as a universal mechanism for generating nonanalytic behavior in time-averaged observables. It reveals that while the underlying stationary state remains smooth, the emergence of a limit cycle creates a 'kink' in observables due to the geometric effects of phase averaging.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating the origin of nonanalytic (singular) behavior in time-averaged observables at the onset of supercritical Hopf bifurcations.

**Main result.** The authors show that time-averaged observables generically exhibit 'kink' singularities (discontinuous derivatives) at Hopf bifurcations due to phase averaging over the emergent limit cycle, even when the stationary state remains smooth.

**Method.** The study uses center-manifold reduction, normal form theory, and phase averaging to derive an integer-power expansion for excess observables, supplemented by numerical verification in chemical, electronic, and climate models.

**Model / system.** A general class of driven, nonlinear, dissipative dynamical systems undergoing supercritical Hopf bifurcations, with specific applications to the Brusselator (chemical), CMOS ring oscillators (electronic), and ENSO (climate).

**Key observables.** Time-averaged observables such as excess semi-grand Gibbs free energy, entropy production rate, chemical work rate, and temperature anomaly variance.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The bifurcation parameter (distance from criticality), the first Lyapunov coefficient, and the oscillation amplitude.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The derivation assumes non-degenerate, supercritical Hopf bifurcations and smooth, finite-dimensional dynamical systems.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 compares stationary vs. Hopf bifurcations; Figure 2 demonstrates the 'kink' singularity in the Brusselator, the higher-order singularity in CMOS oscillators, and the scaling in large-N CMOS rings.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of singularity at Hopf bifurcations, provides a mathematical derivation of the expansion of observables via phase averaging, presents an Ehrenfest-like hierarchy of singularities, and validates the theory using various physical models.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Hopf bifurcations are a universal route to self-sustained oscillations in driven systems. Despite the absence of any singular stationary state, we show that time-averaged observables generically exhibit singularities at the onset of oscillations. The origin of this behavior is geometric: phase averaging over the emergent periodic attractor eliminates odd powers of the oscillation amplitude, while the squared amplitude varies smoothly with the distance from the bifurcation. Consequently, the excess of any smooth time-averaged observable admits an integer-power expansion; observables remain finite but display discontinuities in finite-order derivatives. This yields an Ehrenfest-like hierarchy of Hopf singularities, in which the first nonanalytic derivative is determined by the lowest-order coupling between the observable and the limit-cycle waveform that survives phase averaging. Generic observables therefore exhibit kink singularities, while symmetry or geometric cancellations can suppress lower-order couplings and shift nonanalyticity to higher derivatives. We demonstrate this mechanism in chemical, electronic, and climate oscillators. Our results identify supercritical Hopf bifurcations as a universal mechanism for nonanalytic observable behavior, where singular features arise without any underlying singular stationary state. They thus provide a generic setting for singular behavior without divergence.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.04139"></a>
### [Tunneling from an oscillating initial state in quantum mechanics](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04139v1)

**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.04139v1>
